\startlocaldefs

Exponential mixing properties of nonlinear functional autoregressive models
ShuntarouВ Suzukilabel=e1]s-suzuki@sigmath.es.osaka-u.ac.jp
YoshikazuВ Teradalabel=e2]terada.yoshikazu.es@osaka-u.ac.jp
Graduate School of Engineering Science, The University of Osaka, Osaka, Japanpresep=, ]e1,e2
Center for Advanced Integrated Intelligence Research, RIKEN
Abstract
The importance of functional data analysis has increased substantially in recent years.
In machine learning, nonlinear function regression based on deep neural networks is referred to as operator learning,
and many of its applications involve functional time series data.
However, the theoretical understanding of nonlinear models in functional time series analysis remains limited,
as most existing works focus on linear models.
In this paper, we derive basic properties for analyzing adaptive learning in nonlinear functional autoregressive (NFAR) models.
Specifically, we derive sufficient conditions for NFAR models to be exponentially mixing.
We provide an example with a Hammerstein operator under which these conditions are satisfied.
As an application of exponential mixing, we consider operator learning for NFAR models with Urysohn operators
and derive convergence rates for adaptive estimators based on deep neural networks.
deep neural networks,
keywords:
[class=MSC]
keywords:
1
Introduction
In recent years, advances in measurement technology have enabled the collection of data in which each observational unit is densely observed over a continuum, as in spectrometric or longitudinal studies.
Functional data analysis (FDA), introduced by
Ramsay (
1982
)
,
provides a systematic framework for analyzing such data.
In FDA, a functional time series is a time series whose observations are functions,
arising in a wide range of applications.
For example, a year-long record of daily electricity demand yields a curve for each day, viewed as a function of time,
while a three-month record of daily temperature fields yields a surface for each day, viewed as a function of latitude and longitude.
The analysis of functional time series has attracted considerable attention
(
Bosq,
2000
;
HorvГЎth and Kokoszka,
2012
;
Kokoszka and Reimherr,
2017
).
One of the most important models for functional time series is the functional autoregressive (FAR) model.
Let
в„Ӣ
:=
{
f
:
[
0
,
1
]
d
вҶ’
в„қ
|
вҲ«
[

,
1
]
d
|
f
вҖӢ
(
рқ’–
)
|
2
вҖӢ
рқ‘‘
рқ’–
<
вҲһ
}
\mathcal{H}:=\Bigl\{f:[0,1]^{d}\to\mathbb{R}\ \Bigm|\ \int_{[0,1]^{d}}\lvert f(\bm{u})\rvert^{2}d\bm{u}<\infty\Bigr\}
and let
{
X
t
}
t
вҲҲ
в„•
\{X_{t}\}_{t\in\mathbb{N}}
be an
в„Ӣ
\mathcal{H}
-valued time series.
The FAR model is defined by
X
t
+
1
\displaystyle X_{t+1}
=
ОЁ
0
вҖӢ
(
X
t
)
+
Оҫ
t
,
t
вҲҲ
в„•
,
\displaystyle=\Psi_{0}(X_{t})+\xi_{t},\quad t\in\mathbb{N},
(1)
where
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
is an operator from
в„Ӣ
\mathcal{H}
to
в„Ӣ
\mathcal{H}
,
and
{
Оҫ
t
}
t
вҲҲ
в„•
\{\xi_{t}\}_{t\in\mathbb{N}}
is a sequence of i.i.d. random elements in
в„Ӣ
\mathcal{H}
with mean zero.
Most existing studies consider the case where
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
is a Hilbert-Schmidt operator.
Studies on the estimation of
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
include
Bosq (
1991
)
,
Antoniadis and Sapatinas (
2003
)
, and
Kargin and Onatski (
2008
)
.
Statistical inference other than the estimation of
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
, such as stability
testing and order determination, has also been actively studied; see, for example,
HorvГЎth
et al.
(
2010
)
and
Kokoszka and Reimherr (
2013
)
.
However, classical FAR models are restricted to linear operators
and thus have limited expressive power for temporal dynamics.
We consider a nonlinear functional autoregressive (NFAR) model in which
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
is a nonlinear operator.
NFAR models are closely related to operator learning, which has recently attracted considerable attention in machine learning.
Operator learning aims to approximate (possibly nonlinear) operators via deep neural networks (DNNs).
For further details, we refer the reader to
Subedi and Tewari (
2025
)
.
One practical advantage of these methods is that, after training,
they can provide fast approximations to computationally expensive input-output maps between function spaces.
This feature is useful in the simulation and prediction of physical systems.
A representative problem is to learn an operator that describes the time evolution of spatiotemporal data.
For example,
Kissas
et al.
(
2022
)
proposed models based on Deep Operator Networks (DeepONets;
Lu
et al.
,
2021
)
and Fourier neural operators (FNOs;
Li
et al.
,
2023
) for predicting flow past a cylinder,
while
Pathak
et al.
(
2022
)
applied an FNO-based architecture to global weather forecasting; see also
Choi
et al.
(
2024
)
.
Because these applications involve learning nonlinear maps from current or past spatial fields to future spatial fields,
they can naturally be interpreted as learning nonlinear transition operators for functional time series.
Accordingly, NFAR models are closely connected to practical applications of operator
learning and are an important subject of study in both functional time series analysis and operator learning.
However, the theoretical foundations for estimating and learning
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
in NFAR models are still underdeveloped.
In the context of operator learning,
recent studies have treated the problem of learning an unknown target operator from inputвҖ“output pairs of functions
as nonparametric regression between function spaces,
and have derived generalization error bounds for the resulting estimators.
The available theory is largely restricted to independent and identically distributed observations,
and temporally dependent data have received comparatively little attention.
For example,
Reinhardt
et al.
(
2024
)
consider nonparametric regression between separable Hilbert spaces,
a setting closely related to function-on-function regression in FDA.
They derive concentration inequalities for least-squares empirical risk minimizers over general operator classes.
Related studies have also developed generalization-error bounds for specific DNN-based operator estimators;
see, for example,
Liu
et al.
(
2024
)
.
These studies are also based on i.i.d. sampling schemes.
In the functional time series literature, only a few studies consider the estimation of
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
in NFAR models.
One representative study is
Zhu and Politis (
2017
)
,
which proposed a kernel estimator for
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
and established the asymptotic normality of the resulting estimator.
Their analysis, however, relies on the assumption that the mixing coefficients
of the functional time series decay at a sufficiently fast rate.
As discussed below, verifying such mixing conditions for NFAR models is nontrivial and has not been systematically addressed. A detailed verification of this assumption was outside the scope of
Zhu and Politis (
2017
)
.
Mixing conditions are assumptions that characterize the strength of dependence among observations in dependent data settings, such as time series or spatial models.
For further details on mixing conditions, see
Rio (
2017
)
.
In statistics, mixing conditions are applied to show asymptotic properties of nonparametric estimators,
including deep learning-based methods, for samples with dependence
(
Kreiss and Neumann,
1998
;
TjГёstheim and Auestad,
1994
;
Kurisu
et al.
,
2025
).
Accordingly, the verification of mixing conditions has been studied extensively.
For instance,
Chen and Chen (
2000
)
gave sufficient conditions under which nonlinear AR models are exponentially
ОІ
\beta
-mixing in the finite-dimensional case.
Moreover,
Meyn and Tweedie (
2009b
)
and
Hairer and Mattingly (
2011
)
provided sufficient conditions for exponential
ОІ
\beta
-mixing of a broader class of Markov chains.
However, it is nontrivial for stochastic processes taking values in infinite dimensional spaces to satisfy mixing conditions.
This difficulty stems from the fact that probability measures on infinite dimensional spaces can be mutually singular.
For example, whether a stochastic partial differential equation (i.e., an infinite dimensional stochastic process) exhibits exponential mixing has typically been studied on a case-by-case basis (
Hairer,
2002
; Goldys and Maslowski,
2005
).
Although broadly applicable conditions for guaranteeing exponential mixing in large classes of stochastic partial differential equations remain limited, similar difficulties also arise for NFAR models.
While establishing sufficient conditions for NFAR models to be exponentially mixing is crucial for deriving the asymptotic behavior of estimators of
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
and the generalization error of learning methods, this problem has not been systematically addressed.
In this paper, we first establish sufficient conditions under which the FAR model (
1
) is exponentially
ОІ
\beta
-mixing,
including the case where
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
is nonlinear.
As an application of this result, we derive an oracle inequality for operator learning methods targeting
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
.
Furthermore, we consider
the case in which
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
has the following form:
ОЁ
0
вҖӢ
(
x
)
вҖӢ
(
рқ’–
)
\displaystyle\Psi_{0}(x)(\bm{u})
=
вҲ«
[
0
,
1
]
d
ПҲ
0
вҖӢ
(
рқ’–
,
рқ’—
,
x
вҖӢ
(
рқ’—
)
)
вҖӢ
рқ‘‘
рқ’—
,
рқ’–
вҲҲ
[
0
,
1
]
d
,
x
вҲҲ
в„Ӣ
.
\displaystyle=\int_{[0,1]^{d}}\psi_{0}(\bm{u},\bm{v},x(\bm{v}))d\bm{v},\quad\bm{u}\in[0,1]^{d},\,x\in\mathcal{H}.
In this setting,
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
is referred to as a Urysohn operator and
ПҲ
0
\psi_{0}
as a Urysohn kernel.
Urysohn operators are closely related to recent applications of operator learning to physical simulation.
Indeed, solution operators for partial differential equations, such as the Burgers and NavierвҖ“Stokes equations,
can often be represented or approximated, under suitable conditions, through integral equations or nonlocal integral operators.
Such nonlinear integral operators can be naturally described within the Urysohn-operator framework.
Thus, estimating the Urysohn kernel
ПҲ
0
\psi_{0}
, and hence the induced operator
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
,
is naturally connected to operator learning problems arising in physical simulation.
This connection is also reflected in the neural integral equation framework of
Zappala
et al.
(
2024
)
,
where spatiotemporal data are formulated as solutions to integral equations and the integral terms are parameterized
by neural networks and learned from data. Motivated by this connection,
we propose an operator learning method for estimating
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
by approximating the Urysohn kernel
ПҲ
0
\psi_{0}
with a DNN. We then use the derived oracle inequality to establish an upper bound on the generalization error of the proposed method.
In summary, the main contributions of this work are as follows:
вҖў
We derive sufficient conditions under which NFAR models are exponentially
ОІ
\beta
-mixing,
including cases where
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
is nonlinear.
вҖў
As an application, we derive an oracle inequality for an estimator of
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
in (
1
) under the assumption that the NFAR model is exponentially
ОІ
\beta
-mixing.
вҖў
We propose a novel operator learning model for NFAR models in which
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
is a Urysohn operator, and establish an upper bound on its generalization error.
The rest of the paper is organized as follows.
Section
2
introduces notation and assumptions for the nonlinear functional autoregressive model.
Section
3
provides sufficient conditions ensuring that NFAR models are exponentially
ОІ
\beta
-mixing.
As an application, Section
4
develops an oracle inequality for estimators of
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
under suitable regularity and derives the corresponding convergence rates when the true operator is restricted to Urysohn operators
and its Urysohn kernel is learned via ReLU DNNs.
Moreover, Section
5
empirically investigates the generalization error via numerical experiments for the setting considered in Section
4
.
The appendix presents the proofs of the main results.

Remark
.
The Gaussianity assumption plays a crucial role in the proofs of our main results.
To establish that NFAR models are exponentially
ОІ
\beta

In infinite dimensional spaces, however, probability measures are often mutually singular, and hence such a density ratio need not exist.
On the other hand, when

is Gaussian, LemmaВ A.1 ensures the existence of

вҖӢ

under a suitable condition.
Therefore, to ensure that the density ratio is well defined in the infinite dimensional setting, we impose Assumption
1
.

Remark
.

4
Applications of exponential mixing
In this section, we use the exponential
ОІ
\beta
-mixing property of NFAR models to derive an oracle inequality for learning methods of the true operator
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
.
In Section
4.1
, we derive an upper bound on the generalization error of an estimator taking values in a given hypothesis set.
In Section
4.2
, we address more practical settings.
We restrict attention to the case where the true operator
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
is a Urysohn operator and estimate
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
by learning its Urysohn kernel using DNNs.
As noted at the beginning of Section
3.1
, we derive an upper bound on the generalization error of estimators of
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
by adopting a hypothesis set whose input domain is restricted to a bounded subset of
в„Ӣ
\mathcal{H}
.
This restriction is necessary to derive approximation error bounds for deep learning models, as such models are unable to represent complex functions in regions far from the origin.
Indeed, many results on the approximation and generalization error of deep learning impose boundedness assumptions on the input domain (
DeVore
et al.
,
2021
;
Liu
et al.
,
2025
;
Schmidt-Hieber,
2020
).
Accordingly, in Section
4
we impose boundedness on the input domain of the hypothesis set.
As discussed in Section
3
, this restriction necessitates the mixing assumption.

Remark
.
In this study, we work with a sup-norm bounded domain for operators

вҲҲ
в„ұ

This choice is natural for the setting in Section

,
where the true operator
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
is given by a Urysohn operator.
The estimator is obtained by learning its Urysohn kernel, which is a real-valued function on a Euclidean space.
Therefore, evaluating the approximation error of the operator
learning model reduces to evaluating the approximation error of deep learning models for finite dimensional functions.
Consequently, boundedness must be imposed pointwise on

, rather than through an

-type average over

.
We introduce the following notation. For

6
Conclusion
In this paper, we established sufficient conditions for NFAR models to be exponentially
ОІ
\beta
-mixing
by applying the Harris-type framework of
Hairer and Mattingly (
2011
)
.
As an application of the exponential
ОІ
\beta
-mixing properties of NFAR models,
we derived the oracle inequality in Theorem
4.1
for a nonparametric estimator of the true operator
ОЁ
0
\Psi_{0}
in the NFAR model (
4
).
These results can be regarded as an infinite dimensional extension of
Kurisu
et al.
(
2025
)
.
Furthermore, when the true operator is a Urysohn operator,
we estimated its Urysohn kernel using DNNs and obtained an upper bound on the convergence rate.
A limitation of our results is that Corollary
3.2
relies essentially on the assumption that the noise sequence
{
Оҫ
t
}
t
вҲҲ
в„•
\{\xi_{t}\}_{t\in\mathbb{N}}
follows a Gaussian process (see Assumption
1
).
Extending this assumption to broader classes of noise distributions,
such as sub-Gaussian distributions, appears to be difficult and possible only in limited settings;
see Corollary 3 in
Rao (
1966
)
for related discussion.
In this sense, the assumption is stronger than the sufficient conditions required for
L
p
L^{p}
-
m
m
approximation.
We conclude by noting several directions for future work.
We should derive bounds on the error induced by discrete observations of functional time series.
In practice, data are available only on a grid, and estimators must be constructed from discrete observations.
It would also be of interest to characterize how the convergence rate depends on the mesh size (sampling frequency)
from the perspective of statistical inference for stochastic processes.
It is also important to identify alternative sufficient conditions for NFAR models to be exponentially mixing.
When the nonlinear operator admits an explicit form of how it transforms the input function,
as in the case of a bilinear operator,
it may be possible to establish exponential
ОІ
\beta
-mixing properties
under weaker assumptions by applying an appropriate Lyapunov drift condition.
Furthermore, establishing the minimax optimality of the estimator proposed in Section
4
remains an important open problem, since both the input and output spaces are infinite dimensional.

Appendix C

et al.
(
2025

Our contribution is essentially an extension of their result to the infinite-dimensional setting.
For completeness, we include the full proof in the appendix so that the paper is self-contained.
We begin by proving the following two lemmas, which are used to prove Theorem 4.1.

      should not be a barrier to accessing research. Thank you for your continued support in championing open access for
      all.
